###begin article-title 0
###xml 51 54 51 54 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 59 65 59 65 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
Analysis of single nucleotide polymorphisms in the FAS and CTLA-4 genes of peripheral T-cell lymphomas
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 352 355 352 355 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 360 366 360 366 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 445 448 445 448 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
Angioimmunoblastic T-cell lymphoma (AILT) represents a subset of T-cell lymphomas but resembles an autoimmune disease in many of its clinical aspects. Despite the phenotype of effector T-cells and high expression of FAS and CTLA-4 receptor molecules, tumor cells fail to undergo apoptosis. We investigated single nucleotide polymorphisms (SNPs) of the FAS and CTLA-4 genes in 94 peripheral T-cell lymphomas. Although allelic frequencies of some FAS SNPs were enriched in AILT cases, none of these occurred at a different frequency compared to healthy individuals. Therefore, SNPs in these genes are not associated with the apoptotic defect and autoimmune phenomena in AILT.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Keywords
###end title 2
###begin title 3
Introduction
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 879 880 879 880 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">1</xref>
###xml 689 697 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
Angioimmunoblastic T-cell lymphoma (AILT) is characterized by a systemic lymphoproliferative disorder, generalized lymphadenopathy, and immunologic abnormalities. Originally, it was debated whether the disease should be considered a lymphoma or, alternatively, an abnormal hyperimmune reaction because the fatal outcome was mostly attributed to severe infectious complications rather than to the lymphoproliferation itself. Besides a dispersed cellular infiltrate of atypical lymphoid cells, predominant histological features of AILT include an inflammatory background of plasma cells and eosinophils as well as a proliferation of "arborizing" vessels and follicular dendritic cells. AILT patients frequently exhibit autoimmune phenomena such as cold agglutinins with hemolytic anemia, circulating immune complexes, anti-smooth muscle antibodies, and positive rheumatoid factor [1].
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 238 239 238 239 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
###xml 678 679 678 679 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR3">3</xref>
###xml 680 681 680 681 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR5">5</xref>
###xml 300 318 <span type="species:ncbi:10376">Epstein-Barr virus</span>
###xml 320 323 <span type="species:ncbi:10376">EBV</span>
###xml 340 343 <span type="species:ncbi:10376">EBV</span>
###xml 791 799 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
In recent years, clonality analysis in AILT has demonstrated a clonal expansion of T-cells in most cases. Furthermore, studies focused on the immunophenotype of the tumor cells including their correlation with normal T-cell counterparts [2], underlying cytogenetic alterations, and associations with Epstein-Barr virus (EBV) infections and EBV-driven accompanying B-cell proliferations. Based on the expression of CXCL13 and CD10, tumor cells in AILT were correlated to germinal center B-helper T-cells, which represent a population of follicular T-cells constituting a crucial checkpoint for B-cell differentiation and for the maintenance of B-cell tolerance in the periphery [3-5]. However, few approaches have been taken to explain the autoimmune features that are prominent in many AILT patients.
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 110 111 110 111 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
###xml 435 436 435 436 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR6">6</xref>
###xml 555 556 555 556 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR7">7</xref>
###xml 722 723 722 723 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR8">8</xref>
###xml 797 798 797 798 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR9">9</xref>
###xml 918 920 918 920 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">10</xref>
###xml 921 923 921 923 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">12</xref>
###xml 1027 1029 1027 1029 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR13">13</xref>
###xml 1075 1076 1075 1076 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
We could recently demonstrate that the neoplastic T-cells in AILT homogeneously correspond to effector cells [2] who are by their natural fate destined to die from apoptosis. This is in contrast to peripheral T-cell lymphomas, not otherwise specified (PTCL-NOS) which correspond to central memory T-cells, a long-living T-cell population that develops by "below threshold" antigen stimulation or when polarizing cytokines are missing [6]. The programmed cell death in effector cells is indispensable for the termination of physiological immune reactions [7], and, interestingly, the tumor cells in AILT express the two molecules FAS and CTLA-4 which are mainly regarded as mediators of apoptosis induction in lymphocytes [8]. Furthermore, the neoplastic T-cells in most of the AILTs express CD10 [9], which is a neutral peptidase expressed in reactive T-cells and some neoplastic B-cells after induction of apoptosis [10-12]. BCL-2, an anti-apoptotic molecule, has been shown to be overexpressed in different B-cell lymphomas [13], while it is consistently negative in AILT [2]. Taken together, these data raise the question, why the neoplastic T-cells in AILT do not undergo apoptosis.
###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 111 114 111 114 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 116 118 116 118 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR14">14</xref>
###xml 125 131 125 131 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 133 135 133 135 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">15</xref>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR16">16</xref>
###xml 351 354 351 354 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
###xml 365 367 365 367 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">18</xref>
###xml 3 8 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 238 246 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
In mouse models, pathological features resembling those in AILT can be induced by introducing mutations of the FAS [14], the CTLA-4 [15], or effector-caspase genes [16], respectively. Moreover, the morphological changes in lymph nodes of patients with an autoimmune lymphoproliferative syndrome (ALPS), a disease caused by hereditary mutations in the FAS gene [17, 18], can mimic the histology of AILT.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 113 115 113 115 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">19</xref>
###xml 213 215 213 215 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">20</xref>
###xml 261 263 261 263 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR21">21</xref>
###xml 310 313 310 313 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 528 530 521 523 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 531 533 524 526 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR24">24</xref>
###xml 629 631 622 624 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 633 635 626 628 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">25</xref>
###xml 637 639 630 632 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR26">26</xref>
###xml 679 681 672 674 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR26">26</xref>
###xml 684 687 677 680 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 817 819 810 812 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 821 823 814 816 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR27">27</xref>
###xml 824 826 817 819 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR37">37</xref>
###xml 860 862 853 855 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR36">36</xref>
###xml 882 884 875 877 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR38">38</xref>
###xml 959 962 952 955 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 1029 1031 1022 1024 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR39">39</xref>
###xml 1032 1034 1025 1027 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR45">45</xref>
###xml 1055 1057 1048 1050 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">46</xref>
###xml 367 375 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
FAS, a homotrimeric transmembrane receptor, is an important mediator for the downregulation of immune responses [19] by inducing apoptosis of antigen-primed lymphocytes, including those with autoimmune potential [20]. The gene-encoding FAS contains nine exons [21], and dominant, heterozygous mutations in the FAS gene cause the above-mentioned ALPS phenotype. These patients show a defect in FAS-mediated apoptosis in lymphocytes and a pathological expansion of double negative T-cells expressing an alphabeta T-cell receptor [22-24]. Impairment of lymphocyte apoptosis, in general, underlies a variety of autoimmune phenomena [22, 25, 26] and predisposes to diverse lymphomas [26]. FAS mutation itself has also been suggested as contributing factor in the etiology of other diseases including autoimmune phenomena [23, 27-37] as well as malignant lymphomas [36] and solid tumors [38]. Several studies described single nucleotide polymorphisms (SNPs) of the FAS gene to be associated with susceptibility to autoimmune diseases [39-45] as well as cancer [46].
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 53 55 53 55 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR47">47</xref>
###xml 160 162 160 162 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR48">48</xref>
###xml 164 166 164 166 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR49">49</xref>
###xml 173 179 173 179 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 267 269 267 269 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR50">50</xref>
###xml 270 272 270 272 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR54">54</xref>
###xml 326 328 326 328 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR55">55</xref>
###xml 380 386 380 386 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 427 429 427 429 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR56">56</xref>
###xml 564 566 564 566 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR57">57</xref>
CTLA-4 is a negative regulator of T-cell activation [47] which interacts with its ligands CD80/86 and competes-albeit with a much higher affinity-against CD28 [48, 49]. The CTLA-4 gene has been a primary candidate for a genetic susceptibility to autoimmune diseases [50-54] and to a certain extent to non-Hodgkin's lymphomas [55]. Furthermore, there are indications for a role of CTLA-4 promoter variants in cancer in general [56], and, additionally, one particular polymorphism in the promoter region has been shown to affect the gene expression level of CTLA-4 [57].
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 590 592 590 592 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR58">58</xref>
SNPs, themselves, do not cause diseases, but they can help to determine the likelihood that someone will develop a particular disease. Most SNPs are silent, i.e., they do not exert a discernible effect on gene function or phenotype. They can, however, have important consequences for the individual susceptibility to a certain disease or to reactions to certain pharmaceuticals. In addition to changes in single genes that affect disease risk, it is thought that particular combinations of SNPs located across multiple genes contribute to a predisposition for developing a certain disease [58]. Allelic variations in promoter regions could potentially affect the gene expression quantitatively or qualitatively by altering transcription factor binding sites or other regulatory domains.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 253 256 253 256 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 261 267 261 267 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
Given that AILT is frequently associated with autoimmune phenomena, and given that the tumor cells of AILT show an effector phenotype but-despite their expression of FAS and CTLA-4-fail to undergo apoptosis, we investigated whether polymorphisms of the FAS and CTLA-4 genes may be responsible for these features.
###end p 11
###begin title 12
Materials and methods
###end title 12
###begin title 13
Subjects and SNPs
###end title 13
###begin p 14
###xml 238 239 238 239 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">1</xref>
###xml 383 389 383 389 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 508 510 508 510 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR54">54</xref>
We selected 53 AILT and 41 PTCL-NOS cases from our archives based on the availability of frozen lymph node specimens or peripheral blood lymphocytes. All cases had been diagnosed according to the World Health Organization classification [1] and were characterized by an extensive immunohistochemical marker panel. All of these 94 lymphomas were analyzed for the presence of the five CTLA-4 gene polymorphisms (see below). As controls, we used data of 173 healthy blood donors that were published previously [54].
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 115 118 115 118 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 686 687 686 687 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 820 821 820 821 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 1063 1066 1063 1066 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 1206 1213 1206 1213 <label xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Table&#160;1</label>
###xml 1238 1241 1238 1241 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 1213 1287 1213 1287 <p xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="16">Overview of investigated <italic>FAS</italic> SNPs including references with PCR conditions</p>
###xml 1213 1287 1213 1287 <caption xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><p textid="16">Overview of investigated <italic>FAS</italic> SNPs including references with PCR conditions</p></caption>
###xml 1287 1293 1287 1293 <th xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Region</th>
###xml 1293 1305 1293 1305 <th xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Polymorphism</th>
###xml 1305 1314 1305 1314 <th xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Reference</th>
###xml 1287 1314 1287 1314 <tr xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><th>Region</th><th>Polymorphism</th><th>Reference</th></tr>
###xml 1287 1314 1287 1314 <thead xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><tr><th>Region</th><th>Polymorphism</th><th>Reference</th></tr></thead>
###xml 1314 1322 1314 1322 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Promoter</td>
###xml 1322 1330 1322 1330 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rowspan="2">&#8722;1377g&gt;a</td>
###xml 1331 1333 1331 1333 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR67">67</xref>
###xml 1330 1334 1330 1334 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rowspan="2">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR67">67</xref>]</td>
###xml 1314 1334 1314 1334 <tr xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><td>Promoter</td><td rowspan="2">&#8722;1377g&gt;a</td><td rowspan="2">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR67">67</xref>]</td></tr>
###xml 1334 1343 1334 1343 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Rs2234767</td>
###xml 1334 1343 1334 1343 <tr xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><td>Rs2234767</td></tr>
###xml 1343 1351 1343 1351 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Promoter</td>
###xml 1351 1360 1351 1360 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g-1221C&gt;G</td>
###xml 1361 1363 1361 1363 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>
###xml 1364 1365 1364 1365 <sup xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</sup>
###xml 1360 1365 1360 1365 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>]<sup>a</sup></td>
###xml 1343 1365 1343 1365 <tr xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><td>Promoter</td><td>g-1221C&gt;G</td><td>[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>]<sup>a</sup></td></tr>
###xml 1365 1373 1365 1373 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Promoter</td>
###xml 1373 1382 1373 1382 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g-1194A&gt;T</td>

rid="CR67">67</xref>]</td></tr><tr><td>Rs3218611</td></tr><tr><td>3&#8242;UTRa</td><td rowspan="2">g1107A&gt;T</td><td rowspan="2">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>]</td></tr><tr><td>Rs1051070</td></tr><tr><td>3&#8242;UTR</td><td rowspan="2">g1307T&gt;C</td><td rowspan="2">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>]</td></tr><tr><td>Rs9658776</td></tr><tr><td>3&#8242;UTR</td><td rowspan="2">g1626T&gt;C</td><td rowspan="2">[<xref ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>]</td></tr><tr><td>Rs1468063</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><p textid="17">Different nomenclature inclusive notation is used because polymorphisms were named according to the cited literature. Allele count and frequencies were taken from the denoted literature or, if not existent there, from dbSNP.</p><p textid="18"><sup>a</sup>PCR primer for and rev were used for sequencing</p><p textid="19"><sup>b</sup>no literature found</p><p textid="20"><sup>c</sup>Mutation</p></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
In addition, a subset of tumors (ten AILT and ten PTCL-NOS cases) was selected randomly for the analysis of the 29 FAS gene polymorphisms and three mutations (see below). As a control cohort, we used the data population PDR90 (NCBI Single Nucleotide Polymorphism Database, dbSNP; ) which comprises SNP information in a global population of 90 individuals. To avoid false positive results due to major differences in sample numbers, ten individuals were selected randomly from this database using the "Random Function" in MS Excel. Some of the examined SNPs or mutations were not included in the PDR90 study; thus, control data were obtained from the literature (see references in Table 1). As a general approach, we preferentially chose SNPs which had already been described in correlation with relevant diseases (Table 1). Furthermore, we included one additional SNP that was detected during our sequence analyses but had not been cited in the literature previously. We compared allelic frequencies between AILT, PTCL-NOS, and healthy control samples for all 29 FAS SNPs and three mutations as well as the genotypes for 20 of these SNPs for which control data was available in the dbSNP population PDR90. ###begin title 21
DNA extraction and genotyping
###end title 21
###begin p 22
Genomic DNA was extracted from frozen lymph node tissue or from peripheral blood lymphocytes using the QIAamp DNA Mini Kit (Qiagen, Hilden, Germany).
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 3 6 3 6 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 39 40 39 40 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 387 388 387 388 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 625 626 623 624 <sub xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
29 FAS SNPs and three mutations (Table 1) were analyzed by polymerase chain reaction (PCR) amplification of the exon and intron sections or the promoter and 3'UTR regions, respectively. PCR products were sequenced and compared to Genbank accession numbers D31968.1 and AY450925. PCR- and sequencing-primers used were either according to the indicated literature or newly designed (Table 1). The DNA template, 50 ng in a final volume of 25 mul, was amplified in a reaction mixture containing a final concentration of 0.5 muM primer, 0.2 mM dNTPs (Fermentas, St.Leon-Rot, Germany), and 1x Taq polymerase buffer with 1.5 mM MgCl2 and 0.5 U Taq polymerase (Taq DNA polymerase, recombinant, Invitrogen, Karlsruhe, Germany). PCR reactions were run for 35 cycles in a thermocycler (Mastercycler gradient, Eppendorf, Wesseling-Berzdorf, Germany). After 3 min denaturation at 94degreesC, each cycle consisted of 45 s at 94degreesC, 30 s at the assigned annealing temperature and 1 min 30 s at 72degreesC followed by a final extension step of 10 min at 72degreesC. PCR products were purified (QIAquick PCR purification kit Qiagen, Hilden, Germany) and aliquots of 7 mul were used for sequencing analysis with 1 muM of the respective primer and 2 mul of BigDye(R) Terminator v3.1 Cycle Sequencing Kit (Applied Biosystems, Foster City, CA, USA) in a final volume of 10 mul. Samples were analyzed in a 3130 x l Genetic Analyzer (Applied Biosystems, Foster City, CA, USA). We investigated 6 promoter region-, 13 exon-, 10 intron- and three 3'UTR-SNPs. Sequencing peaks at the location of a SNP showed either one peak indicating homozygosity or two equal lower peaks indicating heterozygosity.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 4 10 4 10 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 285 287 285 287 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR53">53</xref>
###xml 289 291 289 291 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR59">59</xref>
###xml 293 295 293 295 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR60">60</xref>
The CTLA-4 SNP genotypes and allele frequencies of three promoter-SNPs (-1722T/C, -1661A/G, and -318C/T), one exon-SNP (+49A/G), and one 3'UTR-SNP (CT60A/G) were identified following previously described polymerase chain reaction or restriction fragment length polymorphism protocols [53, 59, 60].
###end p 24
###begin p 25
Different nomenclature of SNPs including their annotation is used because polymorphisms were strictly named according to the cited literature.
###end p 25
###begin title 26
FAS and CTLA-4 staining by immunohistochemistry
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 437 439 434 436 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR61">61</xref>
###xml 511 514 508 511 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
To investigate a possible association between the respective SNPs and the FAS or CTLA-4 expression on the protein level, we performed FAS (Santa Cruz Biotechnology, Santa Cruz, CA, USA) and CTLA-4 (BD Biosciences, San Diego, CA, USA) double fluorescence stains in combination with an antibody directed against the respective T-cell receptor (TCR) Vbeta-segment rearranged and expressed by the neoplastic T-cells as previously described [61]. Using this approach, 9/10 AILT and 10/10 PTCL-NOS cases analyzed for FAS SNPs were investigated. Fluorescence images were evaluated using confocal laser scanning microscopy (Leica TCS2, Leica, Bensheim, Germany). One AILT case had to be excluded from the analysis because no antibody against the respective TCRVbeta-segment was available.
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Statistical analysis
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 205 206 205 206 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
Allele frequencies were compared with the chi-square test. The genotype frequencies between different groups of subjects were compared with chi-square correlation calculated on 2 x 2 contingency tables. A p value less than 0.05 was considered statistically significant. Staining signal intensity was statistically compared with Spearman rank correlation to diagnoses or SNP haplotype on 2 x 2 contingency tables.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 138 140 136 138 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR62">62</xref>
###xml 226 228 224 226 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR63">63</xref>
SNPs with minor allele frequencies >/=5% were estimated by the expectation maximization algorithm as determined by the Haploview program [62]. Logarithm of the odds ratio scores between 2.2 and 3.6 were considered suggestive [63].
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Results
###end title 31
###begin title 32
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
FAS gene polymorphisms
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 94 97 94 97 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 166 167 166 167 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 390 393 390 393 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
Altogether, we analyzed 29 SNPs and three mutations in the coding and flanking regions of the FAS gene (six promoter-, 13 exon-, ten intron-, three 3'UTR-SNPs; Table 1). One of the SNPs (IVS4+699T>C) was discovered during our evaluation of the data and was found in the dbSNP database; however, this SNP has not been described in the literature before. Overall, we could not detect SNPs at FAS splice sites among our sequences.
###end p 33

###xml 436 437 436 437 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab2" ref-type="table">2</xref>

###xml 713 714 713 714 <td xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</td>

###xml 525 530 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Three gene loci (-691t>c, IVS4+699T>C, IVS7+312C>T) showed differences in allelic frequencies when AILT and PTCL-NOS cases were compared; however, these SNPs did not differ statistically in their allelic frequency values when compared to the control cases. For four SNPs (IVS2+176C>T, IVS4+699T>C, A/T(735)G/C, c.699(+82)c>g), we were able to detect differences in their genotype frequencies when all three groups were compared (Tables 2 and 3, P values in bold type). ###xml 292 298 292 298 <label xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;1</label>
###xml 322 325 322 325 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 389 390 389 390 <sup xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</sup>

###xml 298 530 298 530 <caption xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><p textid="45"> Cluster analysis of 20 <italic>FAS</italic> SNP genotypes with AILT, PTCL-NOS, and control individuals. ###xml 530 530 530 530 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="12308_2008_3_Fig1_HTML" id="MO1"/>
###xml 292 530 292 530 <fig xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Fig1"><label>Fig.&#160;1</label><caption><p textid="45"> Cluster analysis of 20 <italic>FAS</italic> SNP genotypes with AILT, PTCL-NOS, and control individuals. FAS<sup>&#8722;</sup> cases are <italic>framed</italic> and FAS<sup>+</sup> cases are additionally <italic>labelled in grey</italic>. The <italic>remaining cases</italic> represent controls without available expression data</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="12308_2008_3_Fig1_HTML" id="MO1"/></fig>
Cluster analysis of all three groups for the combined genotypes of the previously mentioned 20 SNPs revealed one subgroup with a high degree of similarities which contained 7/10 of the AILT cases (Fig. 1). The remaining three AILT cases were more closely linked to PTCL-NOS or control cases. Fig. 1 Cluster analysis of 20 FAS SNP genotypes with AILT, PTCL-NOS, and control individuals. FAS- cases are framed and FAS+ cases are additionally labelled in grey. The remaining cases represent controls without available expression data
###end p 44

Not possible because of technical reasons</p></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
To detect a possible effect of the FAS SNP in the promoter region (-691t>c) on gene expression in AILT cases, FAS-staining was performed in 10/10 PTCL-NOS and 9/10 AILT. In general, all AILT tumors showed a significantly stronger FAS expression compared to most of the PTCL-NOS (Table 4 and Fig. 2). Performing cluster analysis of FAS expression and the -691t>c genotype, all AILT and two PTCL-NOS cases shared the same combination of parameters (data not shown). ###begin p 50
Because complex disease phenotypes including autoimmunity may be influenced by polymorphisms at multiple gene loci presumably related to expression levels or the ability of variant protein domains to interact with functional partners or substrates, we searched for a potential risk related to haplotypic differences by performing haplotype and linkage disequilibrium (LD) analysis. We found LD among several SNPs with minor allele frequency >/=5% (data not shown). However, no haplotype blocks emerged.
###end p 50

###xml 363 368 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
We found no significant association of any of the studied CTLA-4 SNPs with AILT, PTCL-NOS, and control individuals comparing allelic frequencies or genotypes (Tables 5 and 6). Likewise, cluster analysis of AILT, PTCL-NOS, and controls for the combined genotypes of the CTLA-4 SNPs revealed no subgroups (data not shown). ###begin p 55
###xml 174 175 174 175 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab4" ref-type="table">4</xref>
###xml 185 186 185 186 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 252 258 252 258 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 462 468 462 468 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
The eight AILT cases that could be investigated showed a significantly stronger CTLA-4 expression on the protein level compared to the six PTCL-NOS cases investigated (Table 4 and Fig. 2). Performing cluster analysis of CTLA-4 expression and the three CTLA-4 promoter SNP genotypes, no subgroups were detected that included a significant subset of one of the lymphoma entities. Comparing CTLA-4 expression with the cluster analysis performed on the basis of all CTLA-4 genotypes and all cases, a completely heterogeneous pattern emerged (data not shown).
###end p 55
###begin title 56
Discussion
###end title 56
###begin p 57
###xml 368 371 368 371 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 376 382 376 382 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 554 557 554 557 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 827 830 827 830 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 948 951 948 951 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 1190 1192 1190 1192 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR42">42</xref>
###xml 1194 1196 1194 1196 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR43">43</xref>
###xml 190 198 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
Tumor cells of AILT show an effector phenotype, which is-in the non-malignant counterpart-associated with a propensity to undergo apoptosis. In view of the findings that tumor cells in AILT patients highly express the proapoptotic molecules FAS and CTLA-4 and are negative for BCL2, a potent inhibitor of apoptosis, we wondered if certain SNPs and/or mutations of the FAS and CTLA-4 genes may be associated with the failure of the tumor cells to undergo apoptosis. However, no such associations could be uncovered in this study. Although six SNPs of the FAS gene showed a differential distribution between the AILT and PTCL-NOS subgroups, none of the SNPs appeared to be statistically enriched in comparison to a normal control population. These six SNPs include the SNP -691T>C, which is located in the promoter region of the FAS gene and IVS2+176C>T, which is a silent SNP in exon 2. The remaining four SNPs are located in various introns of the FAS gene. Comparing these results with data from the literature, three SNPs were associated with certain autoimmune diseases, such as multiple sclerosis (A/T(735)G/C) or Sjogren's syndrome (c.699(+82)c>g and IVS2+176C>T) in previous reports [42, 43].
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 203 206 203 206 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 334 335 334 335 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab4" ref-type="table">4</xref>
###xml 377 378 377 378 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 887 888 887 888 <sup xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 1005 1006 1005 1006 <sup xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</sup>
###xml 1038 1039 1038 1039 <sup xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
To investigate whether the SNP -691T>C located in the promoter region could potentially lead to a modified transcription factor binding site and therefore be of relevance for the expression level of the FAS gene, we analyzed the FAS expression of the neoplastic T-cells in AILT and PTCL-NOS by immunohistochemistry. As shown in Table 4 and in the representative images of Fig. 2, FAS staining in AILT and PTCL-NOS cases revealed a significant difference with a significantly higher expression of FAS among AILT cases. Moreover, cluster analysis including only the status of the promoter SNP and the expression data showed a correlation between this SNP and the FAS expression in AILT, with all AILT showing the same genotype linked to the expression pattern, while PTCL-NOS cases revealed a heterogeneous pattern regarding genotype and FAS expression. Interestingly, two of the three FAS+ PTCL-NOS cases shared the genotype characteristic of AILT, while five PTCL-NOS cases with the same genotype were FAS-. In contrast, the remaining FAS+ PTCL-NOS case revealed a completely different genotype.
###end p 58
###begin p 59
We next addressed the question if the promoter SNP -691T>C could lead to changes in transcription factor binding sites. Because no reports exist in the literature to date, we compared the respective sequences with a transcription factor database (). Potential binding sites were found for AML-1a with a score of 83.4 for allele T and for c-Myc with a score of 80.9 for binding only allele C, which could allow the speculation that in AILT, c-Myc does not interact with this location.
###end p 59
###begin p 60
###xml 440 441 440 441 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
Are the quantitative differences in FAS expression between AILT and PTCL-NOS subgroups attributable to underlying differences in SNP genotypes? We believe that this scenario is highly unlikely. First, SNP distributions in AILT and PTCL-NOS cases did not show statistically significant differences to their occurrence in normal controls. Second, tumor cells in AILT and PTCL-NOS correspond to different subsets of normal T-cell populations [2], which show physiological variations in their FAS expression. Therefore, the difference in FAS expression likely only reflects the distinct expression levels of the physiological counterparts. Future studies will, therefore, have to address the exact quantification of the FAS expression across various physiological differentiation states of T-cells. In addition, DNA-binding studies with AML-1a and c-Myc and the different promoter variants could shed light on the question if and to what extent these transcription factors may play a role in the regulation of FAS expression.
###end p 60
###begin p 61
###xml 28 34 28 34 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 236 242 236 242 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 252 254 252 254 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR51">51</xref>
###xml 256 258 256 258 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR57">57</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR64">64</xref>
###xml 264 266 264 266 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR65">65</xref>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR66">66</xref>
###xml 382 388 382 388 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 544 550 544 550 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
Because certain SNPs in the CTLA-4 gene can lead to functional changes, such as modified promoter activity and lower CTLA-4 surface expression, inefficient processing led to reduced control of T-cell proliferation and a reduced soluble CTLA-4 isoform [51, 57, 64, 65], and because some of these SNPs have been associated with a broad variety of autoimmune diseases [66], we studied CTLA-4 SNPs in AILT and PTCL-NOS cases. However, the statistical evaluation of allelic frequencies and genotypes yielded no correlation between the presence of a CTLA-4 SNP with either the AILT or PTCL-NOS subgroup. Additionally, cluster analysis of genotypes also revealed no subgroups. Even though CTLA-4 expression significantly differed between AILT and PTCL-NOS cases, this again is likely to be explained by the distinct differentiation states of the normal counterparts of the neoplastic populations in AILT and PTCL-NOS. This is supported by comparing CTLA-4 expression to promoter SNP genotypes and the cluster analysis of all five genotypes, which did not show any correlation.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 93 99 93 99 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 173 175 173 175 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR55">55</xref>
###xml 150 158 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
Interestingly, in another study, a difference in the occurrence of the +49AA genotype of the CTLA-4 gene was described between non-Hodgkin's lymphoma patients and controls [55]. Four of 44 cases in this study were T-cell lymphomas, but, unfortunately, the authors did not provide detailed information on this subset. Thus, results between our and the previously mentioned study cannot be compared at the present time.
###end p 62
###begin p 63
###xml 70 73 70 73 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FAS</italic>
###xml 78 84 78 84 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CTLA-4</italic>
###xml 154 162 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">patients</span>
In summary, our study provides evidence that SNPs or mutations of the FAS and CTLA-4 genes are not responsible for the failure of the tumor cells in AILT patients to undergo apoptosis and for the accompanying autoimmune phenomena. Future studies will have to unravel the mechanism by which the neoplastic population in AILT that appears to have an effector T-cell phenotype and is equipped with high expression of the pro-apoptotic molecules FAS and CTLA-4 circumvent the induction of cell death.
###end p 63
